# ArcGIS Pro Essential Training

> ArcGIS Pro is a popular geographic information system (GIS) that combines the power of 2D and 3D mapping with cloud-based sharing and collaboration features. Version 2.4 contains visualization and editing enhancements that make it more powerful than ever. In this course, Gordon Luckett teaches you the essentials of working with ArcGIS Pro 2.4. Gordon shows you how to get started with choosing a te

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188) | 3h 47m | Beginner | 49K learners

### 1. Understanding ArcGIS Pro

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### [Sign in to ArcGIS Pro](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] When you first open up [[ArcGIS Pro]], you're prompted with a login screen.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=4)** This allows you to log into [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com) and do two things.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=9)** One, give you a license, so you can use Pro and also, it'll give you the ability to publish your maps and data out to [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com).
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=19)** You can use your organization's URL, for example, esri.maps.[arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com), or gordon.[maps.com](https://maps.com).
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=26)** Depends on how you set up your organization's URL with [esri.com](https://esri.com).
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=32)** If you do have a username and password with [[GitHub]], Facebook, [[Google]], or Apple, you can tie those different accounts to [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com), so you can automatically log in.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=45)** Makes life very easy.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=47)** Now, what if you don't want to have to log in to [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com) or your organization's URL?
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=53)** Well, we can change our licensing slightly.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=56)** So if we go into the licensing page, we have three different license types.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=60)** So we have Named User, Single Use, and Concurrent.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=64)** Now, Named is the default one, and it automatically signs you in to [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com).
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=70)** Now, we could use the organization URL in here, manually change it, or put in the URL of your portal where your licenses are hosted.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=79)** So you could have ArcGIS Pro licensing on your portal, not just on ArcGIS online.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=86)** The other ways to log in would be a single use license.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=90)** The nice thing about a single use license is that it's tied to the computer you're logged into.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=96)** So anyone who logs into that computer, your desktop, can use Pro.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=101)** So you don't need to log in.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=103)** It just works when you open it up because it's got a single use license on that computer.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=109)** Now, there's a way to float it, so that you can log in to any PC, but it goes to a server on your network.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=117)** So you can have a license manager and it'll go off and see if there's a license available.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=122)** So if you have 10 users, but only five licensing, anyone who opens up Pro, the first five people, gets the license first.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=132)** Now, this is great if you've only got five full-time staff and five part-time staff, or some people only use it sometimes, or you may switch computers throughout the day.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=145)** You know, in the morning, you're on the laptop, in the afternoon, you're on the server, it doesn't matter.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=149)** You can float the license.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=151)** It doesn't prompt you to log in, it just goes to the license manager and sees if there's one available.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=156)** If there is, you get to open up Pro.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=158)** I'm going to go back into Named User license, and yes, I'm going to just use the [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com) site.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=165)** Just leave it there.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=166)** In fact, I'm just going to cancel out of here.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=170)** Now, I'm going to open up Pro again, make sure it's there, and I'm going to log in.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=175)** So I'm just going to go my username and my password, make sure it's typed right and I'll log into [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com).
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=185)** And you know I've got a license when ArcGIS Pro opens up and you can see the new project menu at the top here.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=192)** You can see I'm logged in the top right corner.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=194)** You can see I'm logged into [arcgis.com](https://arcgis.com).
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=196)** There's me, Gordon, and I can sign out if I want to, and I've got a license.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=201)** Now, if you don't have a license of ArcGIS Pro, you can get one right now.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=206)** All you have to do is go to [esri.com](https://esri.com) and go to ArcGIS Pro trial professional license.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=213)** You'll get a 21-day Pro trial.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=217)** This is plenty of time for us to work through this course and you can have Pro before you purchase, try it out.
>

> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=229)** So you'll be able to do all the exercises in this course and you can download the trial using this interface.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/sign-in-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=236)** So just go ahead, download ArcGIS Pro and jump right in.

#### [Choosing a template](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Once you're logged in and you've opened up [[ArcGIS Pro]], you're prompted to start a new project.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=5)** Now, there's four kinds of projects to start with.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=7)** You've got a 2D map, so these are two dimensional maps with just X and Y, lines, points, polygons, raster, and so on.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=16)** Or you could use a catalog.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=18)** A catalog is for managing files, [[Databases]], and so on.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=22)** There's no graphics per se.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=23)** It's just about [[Data Management]] and [[Metadata]] management.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=26)** There's a global scene, which is a 3D map that looks at the whole world or down to country or even state or province, or if you have a more large scale project you're working on, a particular building or neighborhood, use a 3D local scene.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=44)** So the two scenes are 3D, the map is 2D, and the catalog is mainly for data management.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=50)** Now, the nice thing is, doesn't matter what type of project you start, you can add others to the project.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=56)** So, for example, if you start with a global scene, you can add local scenes, catalogs, and maps to that project.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=62)** So you're not really tied down even if you choose the wrong project to start with.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=68)** You can add other data or other map types within the project.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=72)** You can have many maps, many scenes, many catalogs within one project.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=77)** So you're not beholden to the decision you make right here.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=80)** It's just a great way to start.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=82)** Now, sometimes you want to have a temporary project, meaning you're going to just throw away the map when you're done, you're doing some processing, maybe you're doing an import of a file and exporting it, then you want to throw away the project, then start without a template.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=96)** You can add a map as you go and then you could still save it if you want to, or you can just get rid of it and don't bother using it.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=104)** So you have two choices here when you open up ArcGIS Pro, start a brand new project or start without a template at all and discard it afterwards.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=112)** Also, if you've got any other projects you're working on, they'll show up here under recent projects.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/choosing-a-template?u=76281980&t=118)** So this is your main screen when you first start using ArcGIS Pro, but it gets you launching into the mapping world.

#### [Navigating ribbons and panes](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/navigating-ribbons-and-panes?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/navigating-ribbons-and-panes?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As you become familiar with [[ArcGIS Pro]], you'll notice that the menus and ribbons are very context sensitive to what you have selected.

> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/navigating-ribbons-and-panes?u=76281980&t=54)** Now, for example, if I go to the world topographic map, and I want it to [[Zoom]] in at a certain scale or turn off at a particular scale, so say at a million.

> **[9:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=580)** If you're publishing maps to your portal or that sort of thing and you want speed and the data doesn't get updated very often, it's very good to have cache maps.
>
> **[9:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=588)** But in this case, we're not going to be doing that.
>
> **[9:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=590)** We're going to leave the maps alone.
>
> **[9:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=591)** Let's delete this one map.
>
> **[9:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=593)** Delete it.
>
> **[9:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=594)** Yep. Okay, there.
>
> **[9:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=595)** We'll get out of Oshkosh.
>
> **[9:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=596)** So our options for the project these are again, global options.
>
> **[10:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=602)** Just for the maps.
>
> **[10:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=604)** We can choose things like the base map, how we deal with new layers, what the default maps should be in terms of their coordinate systems, their spatial reference, what the label engine we should use by default, what the elevation we should use, and whether we should toggle the feature cache each map.
>
> **[10:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=619)** So lots of tools, very powerful.
>
> **[10:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=622)** It can really speed up how you're managing your data.
>
> **[10:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=625)** If every time you open a map, it's got the right base map and the right coordinates system with the right elevation as soon as you open a new map in your project.
>
> **[10:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/setting-map-properties?u=76281980&t=634)** In fact, it's not just project base, this is global for anyone using Arctius Pro on this computer.

>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=222)** So for example, bike lanes look like lines.

> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=244)** So I'm going to open that up now.

>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=256)** It needs all the other supporting files to work.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=259)** So for example, it needs a DBF file.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=262)** That's a dBase file.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=264)** Now, shape files were created in the nineties using ArcView two.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=269)** That's how old the shape file is.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=271)** And back then, one of the best data formats were DBF or dBase, the store you could open it up in [[Microsoft Excel|Excel]] at the time.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=279)** So all the attributes are the DBF file.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=282)** So the shape file contains the graphics, the DBF contains the attributes.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=287)** So like you could open up an Excel and have a look.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=289)** And then there's other helpful files.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=292)** Like a PRJ file tells you what coordinate system or projection that file is in.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=297)** And there's even things such as a SHX, which is a spatial index that keeps everything fast.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=302)** Now you see all these lock files, these lock files are created because they're connected real time inside of my ArcPro right now, 'cause ArcPro has put a lock on that.

> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=312)** So if I were to remove the bike lanes or bike routes from my current map, let's try that.

> **[6:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=391)** So keep that in mind.

> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/adding-shapefiles-to-arcgis-pro?u=76281980&t=392)** If you ever want to share one of your projects, you have to share the shape files, too.

#### [Rendering text files as points](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/rendering-text-files-as-points?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/rendering-text-files-as-points?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Often as a GS professional, you receive files with latitude, longitude, or XY values in it.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/rendering-text-files-as-points?u=76281980&t=6)** It could be a CSV or text file, sometimes a database.
>

> **[6:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/polyline-layers?u=76281980&t=371)** I did use the gallery for the first two.

> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/polyline-layers?u=76281980&t=381)** Now, I just did this as a black asphalt with a yellow line down the middle, but you could change it any way you'd like.

>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/polyline-layers?u=76281980&t=393)** So using a combination of things like a definition query, scales, like one to 5,000, and custom styles, you can make very effective maps and use your line types really effectively so that it's not that cluttered but also looks really good.

> **[7:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/polyline-layers?u=76281980&t=428)** These are some really neat techniques we can use to render the exact same file.

#### [Thematic layers](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Using definition queries are a great way to filter the data you need and then you can color code that layer based on that filter.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=7)** For example, you can pull out all the major highways and color code them red, but sometimes you have a lot of data that you want to color code and it may take a long time if there's a lot of classifications in one particular feature class.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=20)** Let's look at one like that now.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=22)** For example, the parcels under the nanaimo.gdb database have a lot of data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=27)** So we're bringing the parcels and if I right click on that and look at the attribute data, here we are, attribute table, and I want to color code based on the zoning.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=38)** Now here's the zoning, zone description, so we got single dwelling residential, and so on.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=43)** So we've got 32,000 parcels to color code and we've got so many different zoning designations.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/thematic-layers?u=76281980&t=50)** So how do we do that?
>

> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/extruding-building-heights?u=76281980&t=292)** But for now this is a really quick way to get your data into 3D.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/extruding-building-heights?u=76281980&t=296)** Now imagine if you had data such as property values or crime, you could extrude it based on the percentage of crime or the value of the houses.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/extruding-building-heights?u=76281980&t=304)** So it's not really an elevation, but it just renders in elevation to really tell a great story.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/extruding-building-heights?u=76281980&t=310)** And extrusion is 2.5D.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/extruding-building-heights?u=76281980&t=313)** But boy does it tell a great story.

#### [Editing feature attributes](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/editing-feature-attributes?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/editing-feature-attributes?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Sometimes in your data, not only do you need to edit the values of your feature attributes, but you're missing a whole column.
>

#### [Splitting and merging features](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/splitting-and-merging-features?u=76281980)

### 9. Geospatial Tools

#### [Overlaying two vector layers](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/overlaying-two-vector-layers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/overlaying-two-vector-layers?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the most powerful parts of a GIS is the ability to perform analysis.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/overlaying-two-vector-layers?u=76281980&t=5)** [[ArcGIS Pro]] has a vast array of analysis tools for both Vector and Raster.
>

> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=166)** Whereas when I do constant, it figures at the scale we're looking at and doesn't really weight it or refresh when we go in, it sort of stays at that level.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=175)** Those 25 radius stays the same within that area.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=180)** I actually like the dynamic better in many ways.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=183)** It gives you a better idea at every scale.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=186)** Now you'll notice that the rendering quality can be quite slow.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=189)** If you go to the fastest level of rendering, let's go right down, there we go, it gets quite pixelated.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=198)** I don't know if it's really easy to tell, but those pixels are very pixelated.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=202)** It almost looks like Minecraft in a way.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=205)** But then if I go the other way, all the way up to the best quality, it gets very smooth, but the analysis takes a lot more processing.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=213)** Now, why would I do the best?
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=214)** Well, if I were to plot this or share this I want it to be rendered really nicely.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=220)** A nice compromise is right where it was halfway through and it's a good compromise between fastest and best in terms of performance, and that's the best way to do that.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=230)** So heat maps could be used for crime, but they also could be used for any sort of incident.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=235)** It could be crime, it could be accidents, it could be location of certain bird species sighted in an area.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=242)** You could have a hotspot of those sort of species.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=245)** So it's not just crime.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-a-heat-map-from-points?u=76281980&t=246)** I'm using crime as an example here, but hotspots are used for any kind of point layer to really give you a visualization and rapid analysis of where things are taking place.

> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=163)** So what it's going to do is grab all the data and zip it up and put it into a file geo database for me.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=169)** So all these urban trees, for example, are coming from the network.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=173)** It'll actually take a snapshot of them and put them in the bundle and have it one complete offline package to use.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=181)** So I'm going to analyze that right now.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=184)** I'm not seeing any errors so I'm going to hit package, save the project.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=190)** It prompted me to save, and now it's saving the project.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=193)** And it's got to download all those trees online.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=196)** It's got to grab all those shape files, upload them, and save the layout, as well as the 3D scene, the local scene.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=204)** And just putting it all in one big package.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=208)** There, if I go manage the package, you'll see there's an export ppk file.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=214)** If I double click on that it should open up a brand new copy of [[ArcGIS Pro]] and it will contain all the data that we need.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=223)** Let's see.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=224)** What did it put inside this package?
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=226)** It already knows that there's a map, there's a scene, and there's a layout.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=234)** They're all part of this package.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=237)** Now let's go back to the map.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=239)** And this is really a critical part when we send this package together.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=243)** If we do list data by data source right here, the first, this tab, so we can list by the data source we can see that the urban trees are actually coming from a geo database that was bundled up.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=258)** It's not coming from the network anymore.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=261)** Also, the road center lines are not coming from a shape file anymore.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=264)** It's been bundled up inside the package.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=267)** Now of course the base maps still are coming from the online because they're base maps, but all the data, both the urban trees, which originally came from the Namos Live website and the road center lines that came from my desktop are now bundled up inside of this package.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=284)** These types of packages, when we do share we can do a project package and a map package.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=289)** These two packages will bundle up data and give it to anyone who needs it even if they're not within our organization.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=296)** This is a great way to share data, at least statically.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/arcgis-pro-essential-training-22644188/creating-project-packages?u=76281980&t=300)** It may not be great for editing, but it's certainly great for sharing data to people outside of your organization.
